Jamison Brereton

129
Indra
Paruchepa Daivod─Бsi
11 verses: atyaс╣гс╣нi, except ati┼Ыakvar─л 8тАУ9, aс╣гс╣нi 11
The hymn begins with familiar, and positive, themes: calls to Indra to aid our actual chariot in prize-contests and also our metaphorical chariot, the sacrifice (vss. 1тАУ2), and these themes recur throughout the hymn. But the poet seems preoccupied with more negative topicsтАФnot only rivals and enemies in battle (vss. 3тАУ5, 10) and demons (vss. 6, 9, 11), but also evil thoughts and words (vss. 6тАУ8, 11). Bad Thought appears to be personified as a menacing female in verse 8, and more surprisingly Indra seems himself to have potential bad thoughts toward us, his worshipers, which we must combat by supplying him with good things to think about (vs. 7). Given the forces thus arrayed against us, the calls for IndraтАЩs protection grow ever stronger toward the end of the hymn (vss. 9тАУ11).

Jamison Brereton Notes

Indra This hymn is particularly studded with indefinite expressions: pс╣Ы╠Бtan─Бsu k─Б╠Бsu cid 2a, 4d, k├бс╣Г cid 3b, k├бyasya cid 5a; later in the hymn r├бtham k├бm cid 10d, any├бm … k├бm cid 10f.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, frequenter of sacrifices, quickly enable him to attain his desires, to whom you repair in your car to receive the oblation; and for whom, as he is mature (in understanding) and devout, you who are without fault, entertain regard. Accept his offering, for you who are without fault, are prompt to favour us (among) the pious (offerrs of oblations) as (you accept) this our praise.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The chariot which you, o vigorous Indra, lead forward to gain
wisdom, though it [=chariot] is far awayтАФ(which) you lead forward, faultless oneтАФ
just in a single day you will make it to prevail as a prizewinner if you so desire.
(Thrust forward) (this chariot) for us, the ritual adepts, you faultless thrusterтАФlike this speech for (us,) the ritual adepts.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бdas de show two different constructions with тИЪkс╣Ы тАШmakeтАЩ. On the one hand, abh├нс╣гс╣нaye k├бraс╕е is a periphrastic caus. тАЬmake to prevail,тАЭ with abh├нс╣гс╣нaye parallel to the infinitival medh├бs─Бtaye тАШto gain wisdomтАЩ in 1a; on the other hand, k├бraс╕е тАж v─Бj├нnam is a predicate adj. construction тАЬmake (it=chariot) a prize-winner.тАЭ Separating the two constructions is the embedded tag v├б┼Ыa┼Ы ca тАЬif you wish,тАЭ with subordinating ca (see Klein DGRV I.250). Though subordinate clauses are almost never embedded, this functions as a parenthetical like later manye тАШmethinksтАЩ and it also intervenes between two clauses.

Most tr. supply the chariot as subj. of f, but this makes difficulties with the acc. of g, since, by the conventions of Atyaс╣гс╣нi meter, f and g should form a syntactic unity. I assume instead that s├б here refers to Indra in the 2nd ps. and an imperative should be supplied to make a classic тАЬsa fig├йтАЭ construction (see Jamison 1992); note that the next vs. begins with a stripped-down version of the same construction: s├б ┼Ыrudhi тАЬListen!тАЭ As to what imperative to supply, I generate it out of the participial voc. t┼лtuj─Бna тАШo thrusterтАЩ to the root тИЪtuj. Alternatively, it could be generated from the verb found in bc pr├б (тАж) n├бyasi, hence тАЬlead forth.тАЭ In g the word order of im─Б╠Бс╣Г v─Б╠Бcaс╣Г n├б makes difficulties. If im─Б╠Бс╣Г v─Б╠Бcam is a simile, then we might expect the order *im─Б╠Бс╣Г n├б v─Б╠Бcam. However, note I.121.6 asy─Б╠Б uс╣г├бso n├б discussed above, also with deictic + noun followed by the simile marker, so it may be that the placement is by rule (though this requires more investigation).

Note also that in 5b of this hymn the n├б follows a clear two-word simile (without deictic), similarly, if IтАЩm correct, 8g and 5g (cf. also 130.2, 9). Another factor that may have helped determine the placement of n├б here is that f ends (t┼лtuj─Б)na vedh├бs─Бm and g n├б vedh├бs─Бm, so the displacment of the simile particle would facilitate the echo pattern. Alternatively we might separate im─Б╠Бm and v─Б╠Бcam and take the former as part of the frame тАЬ(thrust forward) this one like speech.тАЭ If тАЬthis oneтАЭ refers to the chariot, we must then assume gender attraction from *im├бm. reflects a separation analysis, but with im─Б╠Бm also representing v─Б╠Бcam: тАЬтАж dieses (Wort) wie das Wort der Vertrauensw├╝rdigen.тАЭ

Griffith

THE car which Indra, thou, for service of the Gods though it be far away, O swift One, bringest near, which, Blameless One, thou bringest near,
Place swiftly nigh us for our help: be it thy will that it be strong.
Blameless and active, hear this speech of orderers, this speech of us like orderers.

Geldner

Wenn du den Wagen, der im Hintertreffen ist, o raschhandelnder Indra, vorauslenkst, um den Preis zu gewinnen, du Tadelloser vorauslenkst, so wirst du ihn sofort zur ├Ьberlegenheit bringen, zum Sieger machen, wenn du willst - das sei unser, der Meister, Wagen. Du Draufg├дnger ohne Tadel - so wie diese Rede der Meister.

резрек. рез ) рдЗрддрд┐ рддрдиреНрдирд╛рдорд╕реБ рдкрдард┐рддрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHear our invocation, Indra; you who in various battles (associated) with the Maruts, are animated through their encouragement; (and are able), with the Maruts, to destroy (your foes); (for you are) he, who, (aided) by heroes, are of yourself the giver (of victory); or, (when praised) by the pious, the giver of food, and whom the lords (of prayer) celebrate as swift-moving and eager (for sacrificial food), like a fleet courser (eager for forage).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Nс╣Ыbhiс╕е = maruts; or, by men, i.e. by the worshippers

Jamison Brereton

ListenтАФyou who in every battle are to be besought by men for your skill for the battle cry, IndraтАФby men for your skill for the chargeтАФ
who with the champions win the sun, who with the poets overtake
the prize.
Those showing mastery set him to succeed as their prizewinnerтАФa
fortifying power like a prizewinning steed.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The exact semantic relationship between the noun d├бkс╣гa- тАШskillтАЩ and the related (pseudo-)gerundive dakс╣г─Б╠Аyya- is unclear and may be somewhat fluid. Here тАШbesought, approached for skillтАЩ seems to fit the context better than тАШto be skillfully servedтАЩ vel sim. (e.g., RenouтАЩs тАЬ(apte) ├а ├кtre servi-efficacementтАЭ). See disc. I.91.3.

The cmpd bh├бra-h┼лti-, here tr. as тАШbattle cryтАЩ, actually contains part of the quoted cry as its first member: тАЬthe cry тАШcarry (the day)тАЩ.тАЭ That is, I interpr. bh├бraas derived from the impv. bh├бra with omitted object. For the analytic version of this expression see V.29.8 тАж v├н┼Ыve ahvanta dev─Б╠Б, bh├бram ├нndr─Бya y├бd ├бhiс╣Г jagh─Б╠Бna тАЬall the gods called тАЬbharaтАЭ to Indra when he smashed the serpent.тАЭ P─Бdas de show nicely balanced alliteration, ┼Ы┼лraiс╕е s ├║ vaс╕е sanit─Б … viprair v─Б╠Бjam, with responsion between y├бс╕е / y├│, -aiс╕е /-air, and the final -it─Б / -ut─Б.

The verb iradhanta and nearby inf. ir├бdhyai (I.134.2) are the only two forms showing the formant iradh. I connect them with тИЪс╣Ыdh (/r─Бdh) тАШsucceed, bring to successтАЩ, though the morphological details escape me.

In g the simile marker n├б is superficially positioned as in 1g, after the first two words of the p─Бda, but in this case the placement is correct, since the simile only begins with the second word, ├бtyam.

Griffith

Hear, Indra, thou whom men in every fight must call to show thy strength, for cry of battle with the men, with men of war for victory.
He who with heroes wins the light, who with the singers gains the prize,
Him the rich seek to gain even as a swift strong steed, even as a courser fleet and strong.

Geldner

H├╢re du, Indra, der du in jedweden K├дmpfen von den M├дnnern zum Streitruf g├╝nstig gestimmt werden musst, von den M├дnnern zum Vordringen, der mit den Tapferen die Sonne gewinnt, der mit den Redekundigen den Siegerpreis erringt - ihn machen die M├дchtigen geneigt, den Sieggewohnten, den Starken wie ein sieggewohntes Rennpferd!

Grassmann

O h├╢re, Indra, den in jeder Schlacht die M├дnnerschar gewinnen muss, um dich zu rufen zu dem Kampf, die M├дnnerschar zum Schlachtgewinn, Die Helden, dass du Glanz verschaffst, die S├дnger, dass du Beute machst, Dich beutereichen stimmen hold die m├дchtigen, dich, wie ein beutereiches Ross.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou, the subduer (of adversaries), pierce every rain (confining) skin; you overtake, hero, every flying mortal (cloud), and abandon (it) when exhausted (of its water) for such glorious deed, Indra, I offer praise to you; to heaven; to the self-glorifying Rudra; to Mitra; (to each) the benefactor (of mankind) for such glorious (deed).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Y─Бvir aruram martyam, parivс╣Ыс╣Зakс╣гi martyam = you mix with the departing mortal, you abandon the mortal;

Martyam = cloud, the skin that contains the rain, vс╣Ыс╣гanam, tvacam, trying to escape, like an enemy, from the hero ┼Ъura; the second martyam = cloud, but after it has parted with its water, like an enemy who has been killed, and whom the victor abandons. [rudr─Бya svaya┼Ыase = to Rudra,i.e. Agni (rudro vai kr┼лro yadayamagniс╕е (Taittir─лya Samhit─Б 6.2.3.2),possessed o fhis own fame, svak─лyaya┼Ыo- yukt─Бya agnaye

Jamison Brereton

For as wondrous one you swell the bullish skin; you keep away every hostile mortal, o championтАФ(in that) you shun (that) mortal.
Indra, this to you and to heaven, this to self-glorious Rudra,
to Mitra and Varuс╣Зa I proclaim at lengthтАФto the very merciful one at length.

Jamison Brereton Notes

What тАЬswell the bullish skinтАЭ means isnтАЩt clear. Geldner suggests that it refers to Indra giving in abundance. I interpr. it in conjunction with the phrase in the next hymn, I.130.8, m├бnave тАж tv├бcaс╣Г kс╣Ыс╣гс╣З─Б╠Бm arandhayat тАЬhe made the black skin [=barbarians] subject to Manu.тАЭ If тАЬblack skinтАЭ is characteristic of our enemies, I suggest that the successfully swollen тАЬbullish skinтАЭ refers to us, primed for battle.

My тАЬ(in that)тАЭ introducing c follows Geldner: some sort of subordination is required to account for the verbal accent on parivс╣Ыс╣З├бkс╣гi, since otherwise *p├бri vс╣Ыс╣Зakс╣гi would be expected.

The placement of ut├б тАШandтАЩ in d is peculiar, since it precedes a series of concatenated datives lasting through p─Бda g. See Klein DGRV I.357-58, though he can only describe, not explain, this effect.

Griffith

Thou, Mighty, pourest forth the hide that holds the rain, thou keepest far away, Hero, the wicked man, thou shuttest out the wicked man.
Indra, to thee I sing, to Dyaus, to Rudra glorious in himself,
To Mitra, Varuna I sing a far-famed hymn to the kind God a far-famed hymn.

Sowohl dir, Indra, sag ich das, als dem Himmel und dem selbstherrlichen Rudra, dem Mitra, dem Varuna ganz ausf├╝hrlich, dem barmherzigen ganz ausf├╝hrlich.

рдЕрдЬрд╛рддрд╢рддреНрд░реБрддреНрд╡рд╛рджрд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe desire, (priests), Indra to be present at your sacrifice, (he who is) our friend, the frequenter of all (ceremonies), the endurer (of enemies), the ally (of his worshippers), the patient expecter of (sacrificial) viands, associated (with the Maruts); do you, Indra, guard our holy rite for our preservation, for in whatsoever contests (you may engage), no enemy whom you oppose, prevails against you; you prevail over every enemy whom (you oppose).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

We wish to seek Indra as a lifelong comrade for ourselves, a victorious yokemateтАФin the prize-contests a victorious yokemate.
(O Indra,) help our sacred formulations to help in every battle,
for a rival will not lay you low whom you lay lowтАФany rival whom you lay low.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Both abc and de are constructed pleonastically+++(=redundant)+++. In a(bc) the phrase u┼Ыmas─лс╣гс╣н├бye (i.e., u┼Ыmasi iс╣гс╣н├бye) тАЬwe wish to seekтАЭ is semantically but not etymologically pleonastic+++(=redundant)+++ (roots тИЪva┼Ы and тИЪiс╣г respectively), while in cd ┼лt├бy├й, тАШv─Б (i.e., ┼лt├бye, ├бv─Б) тАЬhelp to helpтАЭ is both. When in fg we encounter the etymological figure st├бrate stс╣Ыс╣З├│с╣гi (тАж stс╣Ыс╣З├│с╣гi), we expect another pleonasm, but here of course the etymologically related words do not duplicate each other functionally because they have different subjects, though they do essentially mean the same thing: тАЬ(he) will (not) lay (you) low (whom) you lay low.тАЭ Because of this structural pattern in the verse, I do not follow GeldnerтАЩs (and othersтАЩ) attempts to mitigate the pleonasm of abc (e.g., Geldner тАЬWir w├╝nschen, dass тАж Indra тАж gern kommeтАЭ).

The vaс╕е in a is difficult to render in tr. I take it as the usual offhand address to the patrons on whose behalf we, the ritual officiants, perform all our actions. Because of the awkwardness I omitted it in the published translation, esp. since the benefit to 1st ps. тАЬusтАЭ is so heavily emphasized by fronted full genitive asm─Б╠Бkam (also in d). These fronted pronouns were also impossible to render in that position without violence to the English.

The positioning of y├бm in fg is worth a brief note. In f it appears immediately after the first word of its clause, stс╣Ыс╣З├│с╣гi, a standard position. This happens also to be the last word of its clause. In the tag p─Бda g stс╣Ыс╣З├│с╣гi y├бm takes the same position as in f, but since more material has been added at the front, the y├бm is now out of position.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHumble the adversary of every one (your worshippers) fierce (Indra), by your aids, like radiant paths, (to glory); by your powerful aids, gude us, hero, as you have guided our forefathers, for you are honoured (by all). You (Indra), who are the sustainer (of the world), remove all (the sins) of man; present at our sacrifice, you are the bearer (of good things).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Bow down the arrogance of every (rival) with your help like piercingly hot kindling sticksтАФwith powerful help, powerful one.
Lead us as before: you are regarded as free of guilt, o champion.
Carry away all (the goods?) from P┼лru, as draft-horseтАФ*like the
draft-horse [=Agni] with his mouth, (carry them) to us.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I borrow ┼Ы├бtru- тАШrivalтАЩ from 4fg to construe with the indefinite k├бyasya cid; cf. VIII.25.15 тАж van├║с╣гaс╕е тАж abh├нm─Бtiс╣Г k├бyasya cid тАЬthe arrogance of every zealot.тАЭ The phrase t├йjiс╣гс╣нh─Бbhir ar├бс╣Зibhiс╕е тАЬwith piercingly hot kindling sticksтАЭ appears in ParuchepaтАЩs I.127.4, which suggests that this phrase must constitute the simile and the n├б is displaced to the right as in 1g. (Witzel Got┼Н try to avoid this difficulty by construing t├йjiс╣гс╣нh─Бbhiс╕е first with ┼лt├нbhiс╕е, but the nearby parallel makes that unlikely.) The relation between d and e is not clear. Geldner makes e part of the y├бth─Б clause, but pur─Б╠Бseems to call for a past tense and m├бnyase is a present. Moreover, as Oldenberg points out, y├бth─Б pur─Б╠Бis a common self-contained tag. The problem, though, is that m├бnyase is accented. Oldenberg suggests that it is accented because the clause is by its nature a Nebensatz. The published translation should probably have signaled this by тАЬ(in that)тАЭ vel sim.

What is going on in f is unclear, since, as Geldner points out, P┼лru is depicted in a positive light in other nearby Paruchepa passages (I.130.7, 131.4). He suggests supplying ├йn─Бс╣Гsi with v├н┼Ыv─Бni, flg. S─Бyaс╣Зa, thus тАЬcarry away all (the guilts) from P┼лru.тАЭ But this wonтАЩt work with g (as it should in the Atyaс╣гс╣нi template), because the guilt would be coming to us. Perhaps the poet is urging Indra to redistribute the goods of the patron (P┼лru) to us.

This verse is one of the very few places in the Atyaс╣гс╣нi series in which the strict verbal repetition at the end of fg is breached (see also the next vs.). Here v├бhniс╕е should be final in the p─Бda, but has been displaced by no ├бcha. I have no real explanation for this, save for the fact that when no ├бcha are adjacent they go last (I.165.3, III.35.1, IV.34.10), but this hardly seems a sufficient reason.

The g p─Бda is a syllable too short. I suggest that the simile particle n├б has been haplologized in the sequence ─Бs─Б╠Бv├бhnir *n├б no ├бcha. The descriptor ─Бs─Б╠Бv├бhni- (X.115.3) or more usually v├бhni- ─Бs─Б╠Б(I.76.4, VI.11.2, VI.19.9) тАШconveyor by mouthтАЩ is otherwise used of Agni, which makes ritual sense; here, without the simile particle, it would have to be applied to Indra, which does not (hence GeldnerтАЩs diluted тАЬWortf├╝hrerтАЭ). If I am correct, this is another example of a displaced n├б simile marker; of course in this case ─Бs─Б╠Бv├бhniс╕е would be a quasi-compound тАШconveyor-bymouthтАЩ.

Griffith

Bow down the overweening pride of every foe with succour like to kindling-wood in fiercest flame, with mighty succour, Mighty One.
Guide us, thou Hero, as of old, so art thou counted blameless still.
Thou drivest, as a Priest, all sins of man away, as Priest, in person, seeking us.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay I be competent to utter (praise) for the (Soma) libation, sustaining existence, which, like the (deity) to be invoked, (Indra), goes abounding with food to (each) venerable (rite); the destroyer (of r─Бkс╣гasas) at (each) venerable (rite). May that (libation) of itself repress with chastisement the malevolence of him who reviles us; let the thief fall downwards (and perish), like a little (water) running down (a declivity).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

I would proclaim this to the soma-drop that is to come, the refreshing (drop) that is to be poured and that, like him to be invoked [=Indra], sets my
thoughts atrembleтАФthe demon-smasher that sets my thoughts atremble. He himself should drive insults and bad thought away from us with his murderous weapons.
The utterer of evil should drain away lower than low [=be miscarried?]тАФ like a little speck he should drain away.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The vs. begins a little oddly with a solemn proclamation to a drop (├нndave), but in my opinion this is actually indirectly evoking the word-play, esp. common in Maс╣Зс╕Нala IX, between ├нndu- тАШdropтАЩ and ├нndra-, the more natural addressee here. The transition between drop and Indra is effected by the beginning of the next p─Бda, h├бvyo n├б. I take h├бvya- as a pun; though the occurrences of this stem are overwhelmingly associated with the root тИЪh┼л, hv─Б тАШinvokeтАЩ, hence тАШto be invokedтАЩ, it could technically also be built to the root тИЪhu тАШpourтАЩ, hence тАШto be pouredтАЩ (see the differently accented but identically formed havy├б- тАШoblationтАЩ). I read h├бvyaс╕е with both meanings here, with тАШto be invokedтАЩ in the simile and referring to Indra and тАШto be pouredтАЩ directly referring to the drop. Both Indra and the drop stimulate the verbal skills of the poet. I see no reason to assume that the referent is Bhaga, pace Geldner, Renou (and tentatively Oldenberg). The rakс╣гoh├бn- тАШdemon-smasherтАЩ in c may be, as often, soma, but is more likely Indra, given hant─Б╠Бp─Бp├бsya rakс╣г├бsaс╕е and rakс╣гoh├бс╣Зam, both of Indra, in vs. 11.

The repeated final verb r├йjati (bc) is nicely echoed in e by (vadha├н)r ajeta.

The cmpd. agh├б-┼Ыamс╣гa- finds its analytical parallel in I.128.5 ┼Ы├бс╣Гs─Бd agh─Б╠Бt.

The lexeme ├бva тИЪsru, lit. тАШflow downтАЩ, appears only here (fg) in the RV; I suggest that it may idiomatically mean тАШbe miscarried, abortedтАЩ, and the kс╣гudr├бm тАШspeckтАЩ in g is the embryo/fetus. For abortion in a hostile context in this group of hymns, see I.127.3, at least acdg. to my interpretation.

Like the last verse, this one, quite unusually, disrupts the strict final repetition of the fg p─Бdas, with ├бva sravet opening f, but distracted to ├бva тАж sravet in g. I again have no explanation for this.

Griffith

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe praise, you, Indra, with praises, making known (your glory); we solicit, giver of riches, the wealth that bestows vigour, that is agreeable, durable, and the support of progeny. May we (ever) be possessed of (abundant) food, through the praises of you, whom it is difficult adequately to honour; may we attain the adorable (Indra) by true and earnest invocations; by invocations, (offering sacrificial) food.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Might we win with our conspicuous invocation [/oblation]; might we win wealth, o wealthy one, and an abundance of heroesтАФ(wealth) that is delightful and an abundance of heroes.
When he has bad thoughts (toward us) we would engorge him with (words) good to think about and with refreshmentтАФ

Indra (we would engorge) with invocations to heavenly brilliance that come trueтАФthe one worthy of the sacrifice with invocations to
heavenly brilliance.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The pun on h├бvya- in 6b is continued by the same double meaning in h├│tr─Б-, a stem that by most accounts does belong both to тИЪh┼л and тИЪhu. (The standard tr.

only render it by тАШoblationтАЩ here, however.) The fem. cit├бnt─л-, which looks like a participle to a 6th cl. pres. or (so Wh Rts.) a root aor., is formally isolated and requires metrical distraction. Grassmann suggests (on no particular basis) emending to *cet├бyanty─Б, but how would such a corruption arise? Witzel Got┼НтАЩs *cit├бyanty─Б is more plausible but perhaps unnecessary. Lowe (Participles 289) takes it as a Caland adjective beside citr├б-, but this also seems unnecessary.

The part. s├бntam in c at first seems pleonastic+++(=redundant)+++; it does not have its regular concessive value. But it was most likely included here in order to indicate which noun the adj. raс╣Зv├бm modifies. By itself raс╣Зv├бm could qualify either ray├нm or surv─л╠Бryam in b, but s├бntam identifies it as a masc. and therefore belonging to ray├нm, since suv─л╠Бryam is neut. (Witzel Got┼НтАЩs use of suv─л╠Бryam as an adj. with ray├нm in bc is contrary to the usage of this stem elsewhere.)

Griffith

By thoughtful invocation this may we obtain, obtain great wealth, O Wealthy One, with Hero sons, wealth that is sweet with hero sons.
Him who is wroth we pacify with sacred food and eulogies,
Indra the Holy with our calls inspired and true, the Holy One with calls inspired.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra is powerful in discomfiture of the malevolent by his self-glorifying aids, (granted) unto you and unto us; (he is) the tearer o fthe malevolent (to pieces); the impetuous ogre that was sent against us by devouring (foes) to destroy us, has been itself destroyed; it will not reach us; it will not do us harm.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

(Let) Indra (be) more and more preeminent among us with his
self-glorious help in the shunning of bad thoughtsтАФin the shattering of bad thoughts.
She herself [=Bad Thought] is to be harmed who has sought us out
with her devourers.
She will be smashed, she will not wax strongтАФlike a firebrand flung
aside she will not wax strong.

Jamison Brereton Notes

With the repeated pr├б-pra I supply a form of the copula for the idiom pr├б тИЪas тАШbe preeminentтАЩ.

Note the common use of instr. pl. adj. (here sv├бya┼Ыobhiс╕е) with (apparent) sg.

p─Бda-final ┼лt─л╠Б. This interpr. seems preferable to Witzel Got┼Н, who supply тАЬgodsтАЭ with the pl.

adj. and take ┼лt─л╠Бseparately.

As in 4a this clause contains both a full 1st pl. pronoun (asm├й) and the enclitic 2nd pl. vaс╕е. As there, I think the 2nd ps. referent is the patrons, in addition to the 1st ps.

ritual officiants, but, once again, a tr. тАЬbe preeminent among us for youтАЭ seems clumsy, and I did not render the vaс╕е in the published translation

I take the fem. subject of d-g to be personified durmat├н-, with Geldner Others, going back to S─Бyaс╣Зa, take it to be the j┼лrс╣З├н- of g (see Geldner n. 8d), but I think that belongs to a simile.

The opening of d, svay├бс╣Г s─Б╠Бechoes that of 6d svay├бс╣Г s├│.

Geldner refuses to tr. vakс╣гati and feels that it cannot belong either to тИЪvah or to тИЪvakс╣г. I take it with тИЪvakс╣г / ukс╣г тАШgrowтАЩ, as a malformed nonce subjunctive to ├║kс╣гa- / ukс╣г├б- (or preferably a derivationally prior, unattested root formation).

In g I take n├б as both the simile marker and the negative. (This is rather like the haplology of *n├б no I posited for 5g.) тАЬLike a firebrand тАж she will not тАжтАЭ If I am correct this is yet another example of the n├б simile marker displaced to the right.

Griffith

On, for your good and ours, come Indra with the aid of his own lordliness to drive the wicked hence, to rend the evil-hearted ones!
The weapon which devouring fiends cast at us shall destroy themselves.
Struck down, it shall not reach the mark; hurled forth, the fire-brand shall not strike.

Geldner

Sie soll selbst Schaden nehmen, die sich uns mit den ….. ausgesucht hat. Erschlagen soll sie sein, nicht soll sie ……; der geworfene Feuerbrand soll nicht …….

Grassmann

Mit sch├╢nen H├╝lfen dringe euer Indra vor, damit er unsre b├╢sen Feinde z├╝chtige, die Feinde uns zerschmettere; Der Flammenpfeil auf uns entsandt, verletz die Schar der Fresser selbst; Er falle hin, nicht treffe er nicht treffe der geschleuderte.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDo you, Indra, come to us with abundant riches by a path free from evil; (by a path) unobstructed by r─Бkс╣гasas; be with us when afar; be with us when nigh; favour us, whether afar or nigh, with the objects of our desires; ever favour us with the objects of our desires.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You, Indra, with wealth in profusion for us: drive along a faultless pathтАФdrive forward along (a path) without demons.
Accompany us in the distance; accompany us close to home.
Protect us from a long way, from afar with your superior powersтАФ
always protect us with your superior powers. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note identical openings to these two vss: tv├бс╣Г na indra r─Бy─Б╠БтАж, with the final word of the p─Бdas showing very close phonological patterning: p├бr─лс╣Зas─Б / t├бr┼лс╣гas─Б The standard tr. construe e with fg, such that r├бtham of e is the referent of any├бm in f. But this seriously violates the structure of Atyaс╣гс╣нi, where de always constitute a unit. Moreover, тАЬanother chariot than usтАЭ would be a strange expression; we expect the any├бm to refer to an animate opponent in such a construction, esp. if it is тАЬintending harmтАЭ (r├нrikс╣гantam). I therefore generate a verbal form тАШhelpтАЩ from the agent noun voc. ├бvitar that ends d: тИЪav + r├бtham is found elsewhere (I.102.3, 112.12, etc.).

Griffith

With riches in abundance, Indra, come to us, come by an unobstructed path, come by a path from demons free.
Be with us when we stray afar, be with us when our home is nigh.
Protect us with thy help both near and far away: protect us ever with thy help.

Geldner

рдлрд┐рд░ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдХреИрд╕реЗ рдмрд░реНрддреНрддрд╛рд╡ рд░рдЦрдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ, рдЗрд╕ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХреЛ рдЕрдЧрд▓реЗ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдХрд╣рд╛ рд╣реИ ред

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рд╡рд╛ рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрдпреБрдХреНрдд рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН ! Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDo you, Indra, (sustain us) with wealth that transports (man beyond calamity); for, (enhanced) greatness accrues to you, however mighty, (from our thanks) for (your) protection, as it does to Mitra for his powerful protection, most potent and immortal (Indra), our defender and preserver, (ascend) some chariot, (and come hither); devourer (of foes), repel any one assailing us; any one assailing us, devourer (of foes).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Tv─Б mahim─Б sakс╣гad avase mahe mitram na avase = lit. greatness is present to you for protection as to mitra for great protection; or, mitra may be rendered ‘friend’, as praises animate a friend with great attachment, tam sakhyam yath─Б mahatyai pr─лtaye saс╣Гbhajante. Adrivs, voc. of adrivat = wielder of the thunderbolt (adri); but, ad = eat; i.e. adrivat = ┼Ыatr┼лс╣З─Бm ati┼Ыayena bhakс╣гaka = the eater in excess of enemies (Nirukta iv.4). i┼Ыaс╕е parivс╣Ыtaс╕е: allusion to the rains shut up in the clouds; and the second reference, to the seeds shut up in the earth germinating on the fall of the rain, and affording, in either case, ‘food’, i┼Ыaс╕е

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note identical openings to these two vss: tv├бс╣Г na indra r─Бy─Б╠БтАж, with the final word of the p─Бdas showing very close phonological patterning: p├бr─лс╣Зas─Б / t├бr┼лс╣гas─Б The standard tr. construe e with fg, such that r├бtham of e is the referent of any├бm in f. But this seriously violates the structure of Atyaс╣гс╣нi, where de always constitute a unit. Moreover, тАЬanother chariot than usтАЭ would be a strange expression; we expect the any├бm to refer to an animate opponent in such a construction, esp. if it is тАЬintending harmтАЭ (r├нrikс╣гantam). I therefore generate a verbal form тАШhelpтАЩ from the agent noun voc. ├бvitar that ends d: тИЪav + r├бtham is found elsewhere (I.102.3, 112.12, etc.).

Griffith

Thou art our own, O Indra, with victorious wealth: let might accompany thee, the Strong, to give us aid, like Mitra, to give mighty aid.
O strongest saviour, helper thou, Immortal! of each warrior’s car.
Hurt thou another and not us, O Thunder-armed, one who would hurt, O Thunder-armed!

English translation:

тАЬDeservedly-lauded Indra, preserve us from suffering; for you are always verily the chastiser of the malevolent; your, being divine, (are the chastiser) of the malevolent; (you are) the slayer of the wicked rakс╣гas, the preserver of a pious (worshipper), such as I am; for asylum (of all men), the progenitor has begotten (for this purpose); has begotten you, asylum (of all men), the destroyer of the r─Бkс╣гasas.тАЭ

Thou slayer of the evil fiend, saviour of singer such as I.
Good Lord, the Father made thee slayer of the fiends, made thee, good Lord, to slay the fiends.
